name: executing-plans
description: Use when you have a written implementation plan to execute in a separate session with review checkpoints
---

# Executing Plans

## Overview

Load plan, review critically, execute all tasks, report when complete.

**Announce at start:** "I'm using the executing-plans skill to implement this plan."

**Note:** Tell your human partner that Superpowers works much better with access to subagents. The quality of its work will be significantly higher if run on a platform with subagent support (Claude Code, Codex CLI, Codex App, and Copilot CLI all qualify; see the per-platform tool refs in `../using-superpowers/references/`). If subagents are available, use superpowers:subagent-driven-development instead of this skill.

## The Process

### Step 1: Load and Review Plan
1. Read plan file
2. Review critically - identify any questions or concerns about the plan
3. If concerns: Raise them with your human partner before starting
4. If no concerns: Create todos for the plan items and proceed

### Step 2: Execute Tasks

For each task:
1. Mark as in_progress
2. Follow each step exactly (plan has bite-sized steps)
3. Run verifications as specified
4. Mark as completed

### Step 3: Complete Development

After all tasks complete and verified:
- Announce: "I'm using the finishing-a-development-branch skill to complete this work."
- **REQUIRED SUB-SKILL:** Use superpowers:finishing-a-development-branch
- Follow that skill to verify tests, present options, execute choice

## When to Stop and Ask for Help

**STOP executing immediately when:**
- Hit a blocker (missing dependency, test fails, instruction unclear)
- Plan has critical gaps preventing starting
- You don't understand an instruction
- Verification fails repeatedly

**Ask for clarification rather than guessing.**

## When to Revisit Earlier Steps

**Return to Review (Step 1) when:**
- Partner updates the plan based on your feedback
- Fundamental approach needs rethinking

**Don't force through blockers** - stop and ask.

## Remember
- Review plan critically first
- Follow plan steps exactly
- Don't skip verifications
- Reference skills when plan says to
- Stop when blocked, don't guess
- Never start implementation on main/master branch without explicit user consent

## Integration

**Required workflow skills:**
- **superpowers:using-git-worktrees** - Ensures isolated workspace (creates one or verifies existing)
- **superpowers:writing-plans** - Creates the plan this skill executes
- **superpowers:finishing-a-development-branch** - Complete development after all tasks

name: cpts-security-review
description: Use this skill when reviewing or changing CPTS security-sensitive code, including Supabase migrations, server actions, API routes, auth checks, secrets, manager PINs, or Dutchie/reporting endpoints.
---

# CPTS Security Review

## Overview

Use this skill to keep CPTS security consistent with the project's operating model. CPTS intentionally does not rely on Supabase RLS, so application code must enforce every permission boundary before touching production, employee, ordering, Dutchie, or reporting data.

## Required First Reads

Read these files before making security-sensitive changes:

- `CLAUDE.md`
- `docs/EMAIL-REPORTS.md` when touching email or cron routes
- Relevant migrations in `supabase/migrations`
- Existing guarded actions such as `src/lib/actions/brand-unit-costs.ts`, `src/lib/actions/broadcasts.ts`, `src/lib/actions/ops.ts`, and `src/lib/actions/packaging-tasks.ts`

For a full security audit, also read `references/security-checklist.md`.

## CPTS Security Rules

1. Never trust client-supplied actor IDs.
   Parameters such as `employeeId`, `approverId`, `updaterId`, `deleterId`, and `createdBy` may identify a target or audit subject, but they must not prove who is acting. Derive the actor on the server from Supabase auth, then load the employee row and check status and role.

2. Use the full permission stack.
   CPTS permission checks should follow Auth -> employee status -> role permission -> business rule. Reuse existing helpers where available, especially `getCurrentEmployee` and `hasPermission`.

3. Route handlers are public until proven otherwise.
   Every `src/app/api/**/route.ts` handler that returns business data, hits Dutchie, sends email, reports health, or mutates state needs an explicit session or secret check. Do not expose environment values, secret prefixes, internal table shapes, raw Dutchie data, or dry-run HTML to unauthenticated callers.

4. Migrations are append-only.
   Do not edit existing migrations to repair grants or policies. Add a new timestamped migration that revokes, drops, disables RLS, or narrows permissions.

5. Treat `SECURITY DEFINER` and broad grants as production hazards.
   Search for `SECURITY DEFINER`, `GRANT ALL`, `GRANT EXECUTE`, `TO authenticated`, `TO anon`, and `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY`. Explain why each one is needed or replace it with a safer grant in a new migration.

6. Manager PINs are credentials.
   Do not store or return plaintext PINs. Prefer a one-way hash, minimal selection, rate limiting where practical, and audit logging for override attempts.

7. Middleware or proxy is not enough.
   Admin pages can use `src/middleware.ts` or `src/proxy.ts` for navigation, but server actions and route handlers must still enforce authorization themselves.

## Search Pass

Run these searches during review:

```powershell
rg -n "export async function|\\.insert\\(|\\.update\\(|\\.delete\\(|\\.upsert\\(" src/lib/actions src/app/api
rg -n "auth\\.getUser|getCurrentEmployee|hasPermission|require" src/lib/actions src/app/api
rg -n "GRANT ALL|GRANT EXECUTE|SECURITY DEFINER|ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY|TO authenticated|TO anon" supabase/migrations
rg -n "process\\.env|ANTHROPIC|OPENAI|RESEND|CRON_SECRET|DUTCHIE" src scripts
rg -n "manager_pin|pin_updated_at|validate_manager_pin" src supabase
```

## Output Standard

Lead with exploitable findings first. For each issue, include the affected file, the behavior risk, why it matters to daily CPTS operations, and the smallest safe fix. Prefer concrete remediation tasks over abstract advice.

name: cpts-release-verification
description: Use this skill before finishing CPTS code changes, audits, migrations, dependency upgrades, or releases that affect production tracking, permissions, reporting, or deployment.
---

# CPTS Release Verification

## Overview

Use this skill to verify CPTS work before calling it done. The goal is not just passing commands; it is confidence that daily production, labor tracking, permissions, and reporting will still behave correctly.

## Required First Reads

Read these before release-sensitive work:

- `CLAUDE.md`
- `package.json`
- The files changed in the current worktree
- `docs/EMAIL-REPORTS.md` if reports, cron, or email changed
- Relevant migrations if database behavior changed

For a full gate list, also read `references/release-gates.md`.

## Required Commands

Run these from the repository root unless the task is documentation-only:

```powershell
npx tsc --noEmit
npm run lint
npm run build
npm audit --audit-level=moderate
```

If a command fails, report the exact command, failure class, and whether it is pre-existing or caused by the current change.

## Migration Gate

When migrations change:

- Add a new migration; do not edit old migrations.
- Check broad grants, definer functions, and RLS use.
- Run local Supabase migration verification when available.
- Regenerate types if schema changes require it.

## Security Gate

Before completion, search for:

```powershell
rg -n "ANTHROPIC|OPENAI|RESEND|CRON_SECRET|DUTCHIE|process\\.env" src scripts
rg -n "console\\.(log|debug|group|groupCollapsed)" src
rg -n "manager_pin|SECURITY DEFINER|GRANT ALL|ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY" src supabase
```

Confirm no new secret exposure, public debug endpoint, plaintext credential path, or unauthenticated mutation was introduced.

## Final Report

Summarize what changed, what passed, what failed, and the remaining risk. If lint or audit already fails before the change, keep that visible so CPTS has a real operational backlog instead of hidden debt.

name: cpts-production-flow
description: Use this skill when improving CPTS production, kiosk, dashboard, reports, Dutchie sync, floor metrics, or any workflow that affects daily labor accountability and product throughput.
---

# CPTS Production Flow

## Overview

Use this skill to make CPTS easier, faster, and more accurate for daily production work. Optimize for the people using the system every day: operators on the floor, managers watching throughput, and admins checking who is performing or costing money.

## Required First Reads

Read these files before changing production behavior:

- `CLAUDE.md`
- The relevant action file in `src/lib/actions`
- The relevant UI flow in `src/components/kiosk` or `src/app/(admin)`
- `src/lib/utils/date.ts` or the local date helper currently used by the feature
- Dutchie client code in `src/lib/dutchie/client.ts` when sales, inventory, or COGS are involved

For full workflow reviews, also read `references/production-flow-checklist.md`.

## Operating Principles

1. Preserve the desktop-first target.
   CPTS is built for kiosk and admin desktop use, especially 1920x1080. Do not add mobile-first responsive complexity unless the project direction changes.

2. Reduce decisions at the point of work.
   Badge scan, task selection, start, pause, complete, and manager override flows should present only the choices needed at that moment. Prefer a clear next action over explanatory text.

3. Make labor truth hard to distort.
   Time, quantity, worker assignment, manager overrides, and completion events should be recorded in a way that supports trustworthy productivity reporting.

4. Centralize date boundaries.
   CPTS operates in America/Denver. Do not build reports from raw UTC-midnight windows or `YYYY-MM-DD` strings without converting to the correct business-day boundary.

5. Keep operational dashboards dense but calm.
   Dashboards should favor scan speed: active workers, blocked work, throughput, exceptions, and aging tasks. Avoid decorative cards or large marketing-style areas.

6. Make exceptions actionable.
   Low performers, stale sessions, missing quantities, inventory mismatches, Dutchie sync failures, and report gaps should produce a next step, not just a warning.

## Refactor Targets

Prioritize simplification in these high-complexity areas:

- `src/components/kiosk/tasks/TaskFlow.tsx`
- `src/components/kiosk/dashboard/LiveDashboard.tsx`
- `src/lib/hooks/useFloorMetrics.ts`
- `src/lib/actions/ops.ts`
- `src/lib/actions/packaging-tasks.ts`
- `src/lib/actions/production.ts`
- `src/lib/actions/production-orders.ts`
- Dutchie reporting paths in `src/lib/actions/dutchie.ts` and `src/lib/dutchie/client.ts`

## Review Output

Recommend changes as operational improvements, not generic code polish. Tie every recommendation to a business result: fewer clicks, fewer errors, better labor attribution, faster manager intervention, less stale data, more accurate reporting, or lower support burden.

## Phase B â€” Dutchie sync: hardening + loyalty + cron

### B1 Loyalty sync (org-scoped, atomic, durably resumable, no-retry)
- Migration `*_dutchie_loyalty_sync.sql` (defensive, IF NOT EXISTS style):
  1. Widen `loyalty_balances.current_points`+`lifetime_points` â†’ `NUMERIC(12,2)`; ensure UNIQUE(customer_id,organization_id); **audit + update ALL dependent SQL functions** (`create_sale_transaction` p_loyalty_points/v_balance_after, void/return fns) to NUMERIC(12,2); widen `loyalty_transactions` points columns to match.
  2. NEW TABLE `dutchie_sync_state` (organization_id UUID NOT NULL, location_id UUID NULL, entity_type TEXT NOT NULL, last_synced_at TIMESTAMPTZ, cursor JSONB NULL, is_enabled BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE, designated_location_id UUID NULL, unique index on (organization_id, entity_type, COALESCE(location_id,'00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000'))) â€” org-wide rows (location_id NULL: reference, customers, loyalty) AND per-location cursor rows (transactions window cursors etc.) in one durable schema (round-3 major #4).
  3. NEW TABLE `dutchie_loyalty_staging` (id BIGINT GENERATED, organization_id UUID, run_id UUID NOT NULL, run_fingerprint TEXT NOT NULL, dutchie_customer_id INT, balance NUMERIC(12,2), earned NUMERIC(12,2), spent NUMERIC(12,2), applied_at TIMESTAMPTZ NULL, UNIQUE(organization_id, run_id, dutchie_customer_id)). `run_fingerprint` = count + hash over canonically-sorted (customerId,balance,earned,spent) tuples â€” value changes produce a new fingerprint (round-3 blocker #1). `run_id` (UUID) is the journal idempotency key, distinct from the fingerprint.
  4. NEW RPC `apply_dutchie_loyalty_chunk(p_org UUID, p_run UUID, p_limit INT)`: single transaction â€” selects next unapplied staging rows, resolves customers, row-locks `loyalty_balances` FOR UPDATE (race-safe INSERT ... ON CONFLICT for missing rows), computes delta vs CURRENT value, updates balances, journals idempotently (ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING keyed by (customer_id, run_id) reference), marks staging applied, returns counts.
  5. NEW RPC `adjust_loyalty_points(p_customer UUID, p_org UUID, p_delta NUMERIC, p_reason ...)` â€” atomic relative-delta writer (`UPDATE ... SET current_points = current_points + delta`, race-safe row creation, journal row) (round-3 blocker #2). **ALL existing loyalty writers migrate to it**: `loyaltyAdjustmentService`, `referralService` (kills the NaN bug), `customers/[id]/loyalty/adjust` route, duplicate-merge route. Grep gate: no read-then-write of `current_points` outside SQL functions.
  6. `NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema'`.
- Client: dedicated `getLoyaltySnapshot()` â€” exactly ONE HTTP attempt (no retry wrapper/Retry-After loop).
- Engine `syncLoyalty` (org-level, runs under `(organization_id,'loyalty')` lock): validate response (non-empty, schema-valid) â†’ compute value-sensitive run_fingerprint â†’ **match-rate guard BEFORE any application** (round-3 major #3: one join query stagingâ†”customers; matched/total < 30% â†’ mark failed, apply nothing, keep checkpoint) â†’ bulk-insert staging under a new run_id (same fingerprint found unapplied â†’ resume that run_id instead) â†’ drain via RPC chunks until done or deadline (unapplied staging rows = durable cursor) â†’ on full drain update `dutchie_sync_state.last_synced_at`, purge applied rows >7 days old.
- `enrolled_at` never in payloads (DB default; existing preserved â€” tested).
- Config/UI: loyalty tile in settings dutchie page reads org state (toggle=is_enabled, last-synced, designated location selector, sync button), `loyalty` in VALID_ENTITY_TYPES.

### B2 Engine quality
- **Entity scope classification** (round-2 #6, corrected round-3 #5): org-wide = reference (brands/strains/vendors/categories/tags/tiers), customers, loyalty â†’ ONE work item per org (designated credential), lock (organization_id, entity_type). Location-scoped = products, employees, inventory, rooms, transactions, registers â€” products/employees stay per-location because their sync writes per-location projections (`location_product_prices`, `employee_locations`); incremental params keep repeat pulls small; org-level catalog upserts are idempotent across locations.
- **DB-backed single-flight**: `dutchie_sync_log` gains `organization_id`; two partial unique indexes: `(organization_id, entity_type) WHERE status='running'` for org-wide entities and `(location_id, entity_type) WHERE status='running'` for location-scoped; + `heartbeat_at` updated per batch; acquisition = INSERT (conflict â†’ 409); stale lease (heartbeat > 5 min) reaped as 'failed: stale' by next acquirer â€” reaper must NOT destroy loyalty staging cursor (fingerprint survives in staging table, not the log row). Kill-mid-run recovery test.
- Fix `ENTITY_ENABLED_KEY` transactionsâ†’syncInventory bug; add `sync_transactions BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE` + ensure `last_synced_transactions_at` exists in MIGRATION (drift repair); enumerate every mapping: migration column â†” configLoader â†” settings API schema â†” settings UI state â†” engine gate. All toggles round-trip.
- Checkpoint semantics: advance `last_synced_*` ONLY after fully-successful run (zero batch failures); always overlap 15 min on next incremental; zero-fetch success DOES advance. **Transactions: window-granular durable progress** (round-2 major #5) â€” each completed 55-day window persists a window cursor (in org/location sync state JSONB) so a deadline-stop or crash never re-pulls completed windows; authoritative `last_synced_transactions_at` advances only when all windows complete. Deadline is passed INTO pagination/window loops (clean stop between pages/windows), not only checked between entities.
- Batch failure isolation: on batch upsert error â†’ bisect (halve until offender isolated), quarantine offender into sync_log error_details, persist the rest; counters accurate. Unit test: 1 poisoned record in 1000 â†’ 999 persist.
- Transactions atomicity: replace delete-then-reinsert payments with order that cannot strand a header (insert new rows with new txn version before deleting old, or move the pair into a single RPC â€” choose based on existing code shape); window boundaries exclusive-end to prevent double-day overlap.
- No per-record awaited queries in loops (batch lookups).

### B3 Scheduled incremental cron (4x daily until Dutchie cutover)
- `GET/POST /api/dutchie/cron` â€” Bearer `CRON_SECRET`, **fail-closed** (S6): unset secret â†’ 500 refuse; bad/missing header â†’ 401. No session.
- Work queue = one item per (org Ã— org-wide entity) + one per (enabled location Ã— location-scoped entity), ordered least-recently-synced first; INCREMENTAL only: customers/products via fromLastModifiedDateUTC(-15min); transactions from window cursor (55d chunks, window-granular durable progress); inventory/employees/rooms/reference full-fetch-upsert (no incremental API) â€” any entity with null checkpoint is SKIPPED ("needs initial manual sync" in response) so cron never full-pulls history.
- Loyalty: only when org `last_synced_at` null-or->20h; drains any pending staging cursor first.
- `vercel.json`: crons 12:00,18:00,23:00,04:00 UTC (â‰ˆ6a,12p,5p,10p Mountain); `maxDuration: 300` for `/api/dutchie/*`; deadline (~250s) threads into entity loops (window/page granular stops); because progress is durable per work item, a starved item RESUMES mid-entity next run â€” no starvation loop (round-2 major #5). Vercel does not retry failed cron runs â€” the durable cursors are the recovery mechanism.
- Local test: curl with CRON_SECRET (Fable live-verifies incremental behavior: consecutive-run records_fetched << full counts).

Acceptance criteria:
- AC-B1: Loyalty end-to-end on dev (Fable-verified): decimals preserved, enrolled_at untouched on resync, deltas journaled, unmatched counted, match-rate guard active.
- AC-B2: Loyalty tile in UI with working toggle/button/timestamp.
- AC-B3: All entity toggles (incl. new sync_transactions, sync_loyalty) round-trip UIâ†’APIâ†’DBâ†’reload; ENTITY_ENABLED_KEY correct per entity (unit test).
- AC-B4: Checkpoint tests: advance on success, hold on partial failure, 15-min overlap applied, zero-fetch advances.
- AC-B5: Kill-mid-run leaves recoverable state: stale lease reaped on next run; no permanent 'running' rows (test simulates orphan).

# Oasis Cannabis POS Platform

## Project
Mission-critical POS, inventory, ecommerce, and compliance platform for Oasis Cannabis Co. — a multi-location cannabis dispensary in New Mexico with 15 retail locations, a warehouse, and delivery.

## Stack
- Next.js 16 (App Router)
- Supabase (PostgreSQL)
- Vercel
- BioTrack (NM state compliance)
- TypeScript strict mode
- Tailwind CSS
- Zustand (state management)
- Recharts (charts)
- Vitest (301 unit tests)
- Playwright (E2E tests)

## Environments
- **Dev**: nlyrqgosspjefrkhupja.supabase.co
- **Staging**: qebolhqhtwkubqdmvcgj.supabase.co
- **Production**: lesfrjlccghndhmmvmuo.supabase.co
- **Vercel**: oasis-pos.vercel.app (main → production, develop → preview)

## Commands
```bash
npm run dev          # Start dev server
npm run build        # Production build
npm test             # Run 301 unit tests
npm run test:e2e     # Run Playwright E2E tests
npm run typecheck    # TypeScript check
npm run seed         # Seed dev database
```

## Completed Features
- PIN-based employee auth with JWT sessions
- 319 permission definitions across 11 categories
- Full POS terminal: search, barcode scan, cart, tax, discounts, purchase limits, checkout
- Cash drawer management (open, drop, close, reconcile)
- Customer management with loyalty, referrals, segments, groups, badges, configure (doctors, conditions, fields, badge priority)
- Customer detail page (6 tabs: Details, ID & Address, Caregiver, Loyalty & Groups, Purchase History, Transaction History)
- Customer duplicate scan + merge tool
- Transaction creation (atomic across 11 tables)
- Void and return processing with inventory restoration
- BioTrack v3 sale sync with retry queue
- Product catalog CRUD with location pricing
- Inventory full rebuild: list page (24 columns, filters, bulk actions), detail page, 15 action modals (adjust, move, assign status/vendor/batch, convert, combine, sublot, destroy, lab sample, print labels, transactions, audit)
- Inventory receiving (BioTrack manifests + manual)
- Inventory adjustments, transfers, room movements
- Employee management with permission groups and time clock
- Online ordering with inventory reservation
- Delivery zones with point-in-polygon address checking
- Marketing campaigns, templates, workflows, events
- Tax calculation engine (excise + GRT, rec vs medical)
- Discount evaluation engine (constraints-rewards model, 9 entity types)
- Purchase limit enforcement (flower equivalency)
- Sales reporting: transactions, COGS, shrinkage, valuation
- Backoffice dashboard with KPIs and charts
- BioTrack daily reconciliation
- Label template management and printing
- PWA offline mode with IndexedDB transaction queue
- Shared component library (DataTable, SearchableSelect, etc.)
- Full backoffice with sidebar navigation and location switcher
- Register configure system (8 tabs: guestlist statuses, order workflow, customer cards, adjustment/return/cancellation/void reasons, transaction settings)
- Standalone badges system with manual + automatic assignment
- CI/CD pipeline with GitHub Actions
- Marketing gap parity: campaign analytics/recipients tracking, workflow executions, discount time ranges, event images
- Dutchie gap analysis parity: products (100%), customers (100%), registers (98%), marketing (98%), settings (in progress)

## Agent Execution Rules
- **Always use parallel agents when tasks are independent.** Default to concurrent execution over sequential.
- If two or more tasks have no data dependency between them, launch them simultaneously in a single message with multiple agent calls.
- Only run sequentially when a task genuinely depends on the output of a prior task.
- When uncertain whether tasks are independent, assume they are and parallelize.

## UI/UX Design Rules
- **Always build working front-end UI for every feature.** Never leave a feature as API-only or backend-only.
- Every new feature, setting, integration, or tool MUST include a fully designed, functional front-end page or component.
- Match the existing backoffice dark theme: bg-gray-800 cards, gray-700 borders, emerald-600 accents, gray-50 text.
- Follow established component patterns (DataTable, SearchableSelect, toggle switches, status badges).
- No feature is "done" until it has a usable UI that a non-technical person can interact with.

## Dependencies
- @dnd-kit/core, @dnd-kit/sortable, @dnd-kit/utilities — drag-and-drop for guestlist status reordering

# CPTS Security Checklist

## Known High-Risk Areas

- `supabase/migrations/029_fast_truncate_function.sql`: verify that `truncate_ordering_tables()` is not executable by ordinary authenticated users.
- `supabase/migrations/20260205120000_ai_conversation_messages_rls.sql`: CPTS project law says no RLS; review any `ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` use carefully.
- `src/lib/actions/employees.ts`: employee approval, role changes, status changes, and delete flows must derive the actor server-side.
- `src/lib/actions/config.ts`, `src/lib/actions/producers.ts`, `src/lib/actions/settings.ts`, and `src/lib/actions/dutchie.ts`: configuration and Dutchie write paths must require admin permissions.
- `src/app/api/health/route.ts`, `src/app/api/cogs-debug/route.ts`, `src/app/api/dutchie/**/route.ts`, and `src/app/api/reports/daily-production/route.ts`: public route handlers need explicit auth or secret gates.
- Manager PIN paths in `src/lib/actions/ops.ts`, `src/lib/actions/packaging-tasks.ts`, and migration `035_packaging_enhancements_and_ai_access.sql`: move away from plaintext PIN storage and selection.

## Minimum Fix Pattern

For server actions:

1. Create the Supabase server client.
2. Get the authenticated user from `supabase.auth.getUser()` or an existing current-employee helper.
3. Load the employee row for that user.
4. Reject if not approved or active according to the local domain rule.
5. Check role/permission using the existing permission helper.
6. Treat request parameters as target data only.
7. Write an audit trail using the authenticated actor ID.

For route handlers:

1. Require `CRON_SECRET` or an authenticated admin session before work starts.
2. Return generic failure messages for unauthorized calls.
3. Avoid returning env names, secret prefixes, database column inventory, raw external API payloads, or dry-run report HTML to public callers.
4. Keep expensive Dutchie calls behind permission checks and narrow query inputs.

For migrations:

1. Add a new timestamped migration.
2. Revoke broad grants first.
3. Grant only the role that actually needs access.
4. Drop unused definer functions.
5. Explain the operational reason in SQL comments.

# CPTS Release Gates

## Baseline Commands

- `npx tsc --noEmit`
- `npm run lint`
- `npm run build`
- `npm audit --audit-level=moderate`
- `npm outdated --long` for dependency review work

## Production Behavior Smoke Tests

Use focused manual or automated checks for the changed area:

- Admin login and role boundary.
- Kiosk badge scan and task start.
- Task pause, resume, complete, and manager override.
- Production quantity entry and validation.
- Dashboard active worker and stale session display.
- Daily production report generation with correct America/Denver date.
- Dutchie sales or inventory sync only for intended locations and date windows.

## Dependency Upgrade Gate

- Upgrade Next, React, Supabase, and build tooling in controlled batches.
- Re-run build after lockfile changes.
- Check Next.js release notes for middleware/proxy convention changes.
- Do not rely on middleware or proxy alone for authorization.

## Completion Language

Only call work complete after verification has run or after clearly documenting why a command could not run. Prefer a short residual-risk note over vague confidence.


---FLOW---

# CPTS Production Flow Checklist

## Daily Workflow Map

Review changes against this floor path:

1. Employee scans badge.
2. Employee sees only valid work options.
3. Employee starts or joins the correct task.
4. System tracks active time and worker assignment.
5. Employee pauses, switches, or completes work with minimal ambiguity.
6. Manager override is explicit, audited, and fast.
7. Dashboard shows active work, stale work, and throughput.
8. Reports show accurate performance, cost, and exceptions.

## Date And Reporting Checks

- Use America/Denver business-day boundaries for daily production, Dutchie sales, and report emails.
- Avoid UTC-midnight sales windows unless the report explicitly says UTC.
- When comparing Dutchie sales to production, make the date helper shared and tested.
- Dry-run report previews should not be public.

## Simplicity Checks

- Remove duplicate state when a value can be derived safely.
- Prefer one clear status model over parallel booleans.
- Replace normal-path console logging with targeted diagnostics.
- Split files only along real workflow boundaries.
- Keep buttons and controls sized for kiosk use.
- Avoid instructions on-screen when the next action can be obvious from layout and labels.

## Efficiency Checks

- Confirm dashboards do not refetch high-cost data on every small UI state change.
- Batch Supabase reads where it reduces round trips without obscuring intent.
- Keep Dutchie calls server-side, permission-gated, and narrowed by location/date.
- Cache or persist expensive report inputs when safe, but never at the cost of stale labor accountability.

# Oasis Cannabis POS Platform

## Project
Mission-critical POS, inventory, ecommerce, and compliance platform for Oasis Cannabis Co. — a multi-location cannabis dispensary in New Mexico with 15 retail locations, a warehouse, and delivery.

## Stack
- Next.js 16 (App Router)
- Supabase (PostgreSQL)
- Vercel
- BioTrack (NM state compliance)
- TypeScript strict mode
- Tailwind CSS
- Zustand (state management)
- Recharts (charts)
- Vitest (301 unit tests)
- Playwright (E2E tests)

## Environments
- **Dev**: nlyrqgosspjefrkhupja.supabase.co
- **Staging**: qebolhqhtwkubqdmvcgj.supabase.co
- **Production**: lesfrjlccghndhmmvmuo.supabase.co
- **Vercel**: oasis-pos.vercel.app (main → production, develop → preview)

## Commands
```bash
npm run dev          # Start dev server
npm run build        # Production build
npm test             # Run 301 unit tests
npm run test:e2e     # Run Playwright E2E tests
npm run typecheck    # TypeScript check
npm run seed         # Seed dev database
```

## Completed Features
- PIN-based employee auth with JWT sessions
- 319 permission definitions across 11 categories
- Full POS terminal: search, barcode scan, cart, tax, discounts, purchase limits, checkout
- Cash drawer management (open, drop, close, reconcile)
- Customer management with loyalty, referrals, segments, groups, badges, configure (doctors, conditions, fields, badge priority)
- Customer detail page (6 tabs: Details, ID & Address, Caregiver, Loyalty & Groups, Purchase History, Transaction History)
- Customer duplicate scan + merge tool
- Transaction creation (atomic across 11 tables)
- Void and return processing with inventory restoration
- BioTrack v3 sale sync with retry queue
- Product catalog CRUD with location pricing
- Inventory full rebuild: list page (24 columns, filters, bulk actions), detail page, 15 action modals (adjust, move, assign status/vendor/batch, convert, combine, sublot, destroy, lab sample, print labels, transactions, audit)
- Inventory receiving (BioTrack manifests + manual)
- Inventory adjustments, transfers, room movements
- Employee management with permission groups and time clock
- Online ordering with inventory reservation
- Delivery zones with point-in-polygon address checking
- Marketing campaigns, templates, workflows, events
- Tax calculation engine (excise + GRT, rec vs medical)
- Discount evaluation engine (constraints-rewards model, 9 entity types)
- Purchase limit enforcement (flower equivalency)
- Sales reporting: transactions, COGS, shrinkage, valuation
- Backoffice dashboard with KPIs and charts
- BioTrack daily reconciliation
- Label template management and printing
- PWA offline mode with IndexedDB transaction queue
- Shared component library (DataTable, SearchableSelect, etc.)
- Full backoffice with sidebar navigation and location switcher
- Register configure system (8 tabs: guestlist statuses, order workflow, customer cards, adjustment/return/cancellation/void reasons, transaction settings)
- Standalone badges system with manual + automatic assignment
- CI/CD pipeline with GitHub Actions
- Marketing gap parity: campaign analytics/recipients tracking, workflow executions, discount time ranges, event images
- Dutchie gap analysis parity: products (100%), customers (100%), registers (98%), marketing (98%), settings (in progress)

## Agent Execution Rules
- **Always use parallel agents when tasks are independent.** Default to concurrent execution over sequential.
- If two or more tasks have no data dependency between them, launch them simultaneously in a single message with multiple agent calls.
- Only run sequentially when a task genuinely depends on the output of a prior task.
- When uncertain whether tasks are independent, assume they are and parallelize.

## UI/UX Design Rules
- **Always build working front-end UI for every feature.** Never leave a feature as API-only or backend-only.
- Every new feature, setting, integration, or tool MUST include a fully designed, functional front-end page or component.
- Match the existing backoffice dark theme: bg-gray-800 cards, gray-700 borders, emerald-600 accents, gray-50 text.
- Follow established component patterns (DataTable, SearchableSelect, toggle switches, status badges).
- No feature is "done" until it has a usable UI that a non-technical person can interact with.

## Dependencies
- @dnd-kit/core, @dnd-kit/sortable, @dnd-kit/utilities — drag-and-drop for guestlist status reordering

---
title: How to implement authentication in Next.js
nav_title: Authentication
description: Learn how to implement authentication in your Next.js application.
---

Understanding authentication is crucial for protecting your application's data. This page will guide you through what React and Next.js features to use to implement auth.

Before starting, it helps to break down the process into three concepts:

1. **[Authentication](#authentication)**: Verifies if the user is who they say they are. It requires the user to prove their identity with something they have, such as a username and password.
2. **[Session Management](#session-management)**: Tracks the user's auth state across requests.
3. **[Authorization](#authorization)**: Decides what routes and data the user can access.

This diagram shows the authentication flow using React and Next.js features:

<Image
  alt="Diagram showing the authentication flow with React and Next.js features"
  srcLight="/docs/light/authentication-overview.png"
  srcDark="/docs/dark/authentication-overview.png"
  width="1600"
  height="1383"
/>

The examples on this page walk through basic username and password auth for educational purposes. While you can implement a custom auth solution, for increased security and simplicity, we recommend using an authentication library. These offer built-in solutions for authentication, session management, and authorization, as well as additional features such as social logins, multi-factor authentication, and role-based access control. You can find a list in the [Auth Libraries](#auth-libraries) section.

## Authentication

<AppOnly>

### Sign-up and login functionality

You can use the [`<form>`](https://react.dev/reference/react-dom/components/form) element with React's [Server Actions](/docs/app/getting-started/mutating-data) and `useActionState` to capture user credentials, validate form fields, and call your Authentication Provider's API or database.

Since Server Actions always execute on the server, they provide a secure environment for handling authentication logic.

Here are the steps to implement signup/login functionality:

#### 1. Capture user credentials

To capture user credentials, create a form that invokes a Server Action on submission. For example, a signup form that accepts the user's name, email, and password:

```tsx filename="app/ui/signup-form.tsx" switcher
import { signup } from '@/app/actions/auth'

export function SignupForm() {
  return (
    <form action={signup}>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="name">Name</label>
        <input id="name" name="name" placeholder="Name" />
      </div>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="email">Email</label>
        <input id="email" name="email" type="email" placeholder="Email" />
      </div>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="password">Password</label>
        <input id="password" name="password" type="password" />
      </div>
      <button type="submit">Sign Up</button>
    </form>
  )
}
```

```jsx filename="app/ui/signup-form.js" switcher
import { signup } from '@/app/actions/auth'

export function SignupForm() {
  return (
    <form action={signup}>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="name">Name</label>
        <input id="name" name="name" placeholder="Name" />
      </div>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="email">Email</label>
        <input id="email" name="email" type="email" placeholder="Email" />
      </div>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="password">Password</label>
        <input id="password" name="password" type="password" />
      </div>
      <button type="submit">Sign Up</button>
    </form>
  )
}
```

```tsx filename="app/actions/auth.ts" switcher
export async function signup(formData: FormData) {}
```

```jsx filename="app/actions/auth.js" switcher
export async function signup(formData) {}
```

#### 2. Validate form fields on the server

Use the Server Action to validate the form fields on the server. If your authentication provider doesn't provide form validation, you can use a schema validation library like [Zod](https://zod.dev/) or [Yup](https://github.com/jquense/yup).

Using Zod as an example, you can define a form schema with appropriate error messages:

```ts filename="app/lib/definitions.ts" switcher
import * as z from 'zod'

export const SignupFormSchema = z.object({
  name: z
    .string()
    .min(2, { error: 'Name must be at least 2 characters long.' })
    .trim(),
  email: z.email({ error: 'Please enter a valid email.' }).trim(),
  password: z
    .string()
    .min(8, { error: 'Be at least 8 characters long' })
    .regex(/[a-zA-Z]/, { error: 'Contain at least one letter.' })
    .regex(/[0-9]/, { error: 'Contain at least one number.' })
    .regex(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/, {
      error: 'Contain at least one special character.',
    })
    .trim(),
})

export type FormState =
  | {
      errors?: {
        name?: string[]
        email?: string[]
        password?: string[]
      }
      message?: string
    }
  | undefined
```

```js filename="app/lib/definitions.js" switcher
import * as z from 'zod'

export const SignupFormSchema = z.object({
  name: z
    .string()
    .min(2, { error: 'Name must be at least 2 characters long.' })
    .trim(),
  email: z.email({ error: 'Please enter a valid email.' }).trim(),
  password: z
    .string()
    .min(8, { error: 'Be at least 8 characters long' })
    .regex(/[a-zA-Z]/, { error: 'Contain at least one letter.' })
    .regex(/[0-9]/, { error: 'Contain at least one number.' })
    .regex(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/, {
      error: 'Contain at least one special character.',
    })
    .trim(),
})
```

To prevent unnecessary calls to your authentication provider's API or database, you can `return` early in the Server Action if any form fields do not match the defined schema.

```ts filename="app/actions/auth.ts" switcher
import { SignupFormSchema, FormState } from '@/app/lib/definitions'

export async function signup(state: FormState, formData: FormData) {
  // Validate form fields
  const validatedFields = SignupFormSchema.safeParse({
    name: formData.get('name'),
    email: formData.get('email'),
    password: formData.get('password'),
  })

  // If any form fields are invalid, return early
  if (!validatedFields.success) {
    return {
      errors: validatedFields.error.flatten().fieldErrors,
    }
  }

  // Call the provider or db to create a user...
}
```

```js filename="app/actions/auth.js" switcher
import { SignupFormSchema } from '@/app/lib/definitions'

export async function signup(state, formData) {
  // Validate form fields
  const validatedFields = SignupFormSchema.safeParse({
    name: formData.get('name'),
    email: formData.get('email'),
    password: formData.get('password'),
  })

  // If any form fields are invalid, return early
  if (!validatedFields.success) {
    return {
      errors: validatedFields.error.flatten().fieldErrors,
    }
  }

  // Call the provider or db to create a user...
}
```

Back in your `<SignupForm />`, you can use React's `useActionState` hook to display validation errors while the form is submitting:

```tsx filename="app/ui/signup-form.tsx" switcher highlight={7,15,21,27-36}
'use client'

import { signup } from '@/app/actions/auth'
import { useActionState } from 'react'

export default function SignupForm() {
  const [state, action, pending] = useActionState(signup, undefined)

  return (
    <form action={action}>
      <div>
        <label htmlFor="name">Name</label>
        <input id="name" name="name" placeholder="Name" />
      </div>
      {state?.errors?.name && <p>{state.errors.name}</p>}

      <div>
        <label htmlFor="email">Email</label>
        <input id="email" name="email" placeholder="Email" />
      </div>
      {state?.errors?.email && <p>{state.errors.email}</p>}

      <div>
        <label htmlFor="password">Password</label>
        <input id="password" name="password" type="password" />
      </div>
      {state?.errors?.password && (
        <div>
          <p>Password must:</p>
          <ul>
            {state.errors.password.map((error) => (
              <li key={error}>- {error}</li>
            ))}
          </ul>
        </div>
      )}
      <button disabled={pending} type="submit">
        Sign Up
      </button>
    </form>
  )
}
```

```jsx filename="app/ui/signup-form.js" switcher highlight={7,15,21,27-36}
'use client'

      <div>

      </div>
```
